  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_7c591c5f-1a1a-4072-b4fd-b6adae4668cf'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer17418878723231791303">»Ich bin ein Känguru - und Marc-Uwe ist mein Mitbewohner und Chronist. Nur manches, was er über mich erzählt, stimmt.   <span id="freeText17418878723231791303" style="display:none">»Ich bin ein Känguru - und Marc-Uwe ist mein Mitbewohner und Chronist. Nur manches, was er über mich erzählt, stimmt. Zum Beispiel, dass ich mal beim Vietcong war. Das Allermeiste jedoch ist übertrieben, verdreht oder gelogen! Aber ich darf nicht meckern. Wir gehen zusammen essen und ins Kino, und ich muss nix bezahlen.« Mal bissig, mal verschroben, dann wieder liebevoll ironisch wird der Alltag eines ungewöhnlichen Duos beleuchtet. Völlig absurd und ein großer Lesespaß.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer175921891" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15092512565319674749">The ideal book to read when you're on the bus and only have a couple of minutes since the chapters are so short - only I shouted with laughter rather often, so that might be a bit embarrassing. I read it in two hours tops. Still: it gets infinitely better once you've been to a performance of Marc-Uwe Kling and actually <i>heard</i> him read the passages aloud; his voice and intonation are a major factor to the hilarity of these stories.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2719931656" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer8751423932422864343">I listen to comedy German books to improve my German and also to understand better the German culture and humor. A colleague of fine recommended this as a "classic". It's a book on politics, sociology and a bit of philosophy presented in the witty humorous diaries of a man and his Kangaroo friend.<br/><br/>Positive:<br/>- It will help improve your German skills.<br/>- Will also give you insights into German society and how they perceive several concepts such as capitalism, the police, friendship, privacy...etc.<br/>- It</span>
  <span id="freeText8751423932422864343" style="display:none">I listen to comedy German books to improve my German and also to understand better the German culture and humor. A colleague of fine recommended this as a "classic". It's a book on politics, sociology and a bit of philosophy presented in the witty humorous diaries of a man and his Kangaroo friend.<br /><br />Positive:<br />- It will help improve your German skills.<br />- Will also give you insights into German society and how they perceive several concepts such as capitalism, the police, friendship, privacy...etc.<br />- It did make me smile a couple of time.<br /><br />Negatives, IMO:<br />- The humor is just old, recycled and I would even say "lazy". Maybe just not advanced, a bit primitive. It very much reminds me of British shows from the 80s!! you can see the jokes coming a mile a way and most of them sound so familiar I started to wonder if the author is just rehashing jokes and ideas from other languages/cultures and presenting them in German! <br />- Occasionally (not often), it sounds pretentious and pseudo-intellectual.<br />- Mostly, it is just not funny! the comedy is built on the kangaroo, meaning, if you replace the kangaroo with another person, then it's just "meh".<br />- Teenage attitude, "sarcasm is the lowest form of wit", when a big bulk of the humor is abotu being cynical, sarcastic and apathetic, it becomes lazy, repetitive and predictable!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="8751423932422864343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17044961844293529083"><br/>A nameless, speaking, Marxist/anti-capitalistic kangaroo and the narrator Marc-Uwe share a flat in Berlin. Very strange. One can and should expect a funny book. Laughter is imperative. So I did laugh.<br/><br/>Some points of the eighty flash-fiction-stories (on 271 pages) are really hilarious. Unfortunately it wears out after a while and the kind of humor is almost always the same.   <span id="freeText17044961844293529083" style="display:none"><br>A nameless, speaking, Marxist/anti-capitalistic kangaroo and the narrator Marc-Uwe share a flat in Berlin. Very strange. One can and should expect a funny book. Laughter is imperative. So I did laugh.<br><br>Some points of the eighty flash-fiction-stories (on 271 pages) are really hilarious. Unfortunately it wears out after a while and the kind of humor is almost always the same. The best way to read this book is only in small bites, otherwise the appetite goes by pretty fast.<br><br>I would probably not have bought the book myself; the whole trilogy was a birthday present. So I'm going to read some more of this crazy kangaroo.<br><br><a href="http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-sa/3.0/" rel="nofollow noopener">

  <span id="freeText3301685792050654329" style="display:none">WHAT A GREAT BOOK GUYS... and you are in for a treat of a review &lt;3<br /><br />First off, I'd like to start by saying that I was about to dub this a 4 our of 5 stars book, but the ending swept me off my feet! ... <div id="review_3132291583" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3132291583" />
    <a title="Craig Dickson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/67554860-craig-dickson"><img alt="Craig Dickson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1536704209p2/67554860.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3132291583?book_show_action=true">Feb 04, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Craig Dickson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Craig Dickson" href="/user/show/67554860-craig-dickson">Craig Dickson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3132291583" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13639671638148217491">The Kangaroo Chronicles<br/><br/>This is the first novel I've read in German, so I am feeling quite smug right now. In around one week I had this book suggested or recommended to me around three times, in person and by Internet robots. When that happens I usually take notice, and as I'm trying to broaden my media diet to include more German language material, I figured I'd give this a try.<br/><br/>This was a good choice for my first German novel, as each 'chronicle' is short (3-5 pages), the book itself is funny a</span>
  <span id="freeText13639671638148217491" style="display:none">The Kangaroo Chronicles<br /><br />This is the first novel I've read in German, so I am feeling quite smug right now. In around one week I had this book suggested or recommended to me around three times, in person and by Internet robots. When that happens I usually take notice, and as I'm trying to broaden my media diet to include more German language material, I figured I'd give this a try.<br /><br />This was a good choice for my first German novel, as each 'chronicle' is short (3-5 pages), the book itself is funny and there are rarely Thomas Mann-style page-long sentences. I read it on my kindle which I'd loaded with a German / English dictionary, this came in very handy for lots of words, although the Kangaroo speaks very colloquial German so there were lots of words I couldn't confirm in the dictionary. I then had to use my context clues!<br /><br />The book itself was really good and very funny. It's written autobiographically, where Marc-Uwe Kling has a kangaroo move in next door, and eventually move in with him. The kangaroo is a very enjoyable character, but it must be said he is a terrible asshole. That's part of what's so enjoyable about him. He is a communist (maoist) and fought in the Viet Cong (or so he claims) and often rails against the evils of capitalism and bourgeois concepts. He particularly rails against bourgeois concepts like debt when he happens to owe Marc-Uwe €4.95 for a toy that he bought.<br /><br />Each chronicle is a brief episode, ranging from one conversation to some kind of event of varying degrees of ludicrousness. They're usually very entertaining and I enjoyed it very much. I'm sure there were many references or bits of word play that went over my head, but these were compensated for by the way that when I get a joke in my second language, the smugness I feel from understanding it adds an extra frisson.<br /><br />Anyway, this was a good time and I enjoyed it very much! There are two more in this series, and I plan to get to them sometime soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13639671638148217491" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1982805114?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Veli-Pekka Suuronen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Veli-Pekka Suuronen" href="/user/show/62084236-veli-pekka-suuronen">Veli-Pekka Suuronen</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1982805114" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer15483951929020604109">I heard about Marc-Uwe Kling from a German colleague, who also found out that there's an English translation of The Kangaroo Chronicles, as my German is not nearly good enough to read books in. The English translation also includes some witty translator's notes.<br/><br/>After reading this, I'm happy that this got recommended, as the book was extremely entertaining. It's not so much a story as it is a collection of clever short pieces, where in addition to funny dialogue and events it includes humor about</span>
  <span id="freeText15483951929020604109" style="display:none">I heard about Marc-Uwe Kling from a German colleague, who also found out that there's an English translation of The Kangaroo Chronicles, as my German is not nearly good enough to read books in. The English translation also includes some witty translator's notes.<br /><br />After reading this, I'm happy that this got recommended, as the book was extremely entertaining. It's not so much a story as it is a collection of clever short pieces, where in addition to funny dialogue and events it includes humor about the writing process itself, but I won't go too deep into that to avoid spoilers. The collection of short stories was perfect for business travel reading, where you can from time to time read another piece in a few minutes of spare time you have regularly.<br /><br />I was warned that I might need to be familiar with German culture, but for a Finn like me, it was kind of easy to relate having grown up between east and west. Much of the humor is quite political and critical of society and I think if you would like to look hard, there could be also something profound hidden under the humor, but you don't need to do that to feel entertained by the book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15483951929020604109" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13466890013699171681">I think I noticed this book (or another one in the series) when they were mmm new in the bookshops, but I wasn't so curious about it back then. Someone ;) recommended to me one YouTube clip of the author and admittedly it was quite funny.<br/><br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h5MJn_Yy7aA'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=h5MJn...</a> (starting at minute 49 it is super funny)<br/><br/>So is this book.   <span id="freeText13466890013699171681" style="display:none">I think I noticed this book (or another one in the series) when they were mmm new in the bookshops, but I wasn't so curious about it back then. My highlists were the visits to the psychologist. No spoilers. ;)<br />Equally fun were the linguistic bits and I liked a lot the written/ spoken language/ dialect I found in the book.<br />I am thinking of the next book in the series as well.<br />The chapters are mostly super short. The book doesn't have ”action” *per se*, as you would expect it in a novel.</span>

<div id="review_1484699312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1484699312" />
    <a title="Woflmao" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27172446-woflmao"><img alt="Woflmao" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1392294770p2/27172446.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1484699312?book_show_action=true">Dec 29, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Woflmao" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Woflmao" href="/user/show/27172446-woflmao">Woflmao</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27172446-woflmao?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1484699312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2499957336656376355">This book is an easy read and reasonably entertaining. It mixes humour with mild left-wing social criticism, together with some ironic self-reflection. It is a classical case of "animal humor", which is funny because placing an animal in these situations is so absurd, but would not be very funny if the same thing happened to a human being.</span>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_2069520019" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2069520019" />
    <a title="René Roth" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/69726692-ren-roth"><img alt="René Roth" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519888941p2/69726692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2069520019?book_show_action=true">Sep 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="René Roth" class="user" itemprop="url" name="René Roth" href="/user/show/69726692-ren-roth">René Roth</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2069520019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11674013765867250547">Neither funny nor a fun read, his performances are more enjoyable. The constant political moralizing through the deliberately unlikable titular character only serves to make the book even more of a chore to read.<br/><br/>This review is highly subjective. If you like Kling's humor, you'll have heaps of fun with this series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2470414108?book_show_action=true">Sep 16, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jose" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jose" href="/user/show/1855450-jose">Jose</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1855450-jose?shelf=german">german</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1855450-jose?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2470414108" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1006994296490984979">This book is a collection of sketches about a stand-in for the author an a kangaroo. The kangaroo moves next door and calls himself a Communist. <br/>They develop an odd relationship in which Marc-Uwe basically pays for everything and the kangaroo pontificates, weasels and fights against the system, with little effect. The passive Marc-Uwe seems to enjoy the symbiotic friendship that allows him to step out and trespass. Some funny situations ensue. <br/>One suspects the Kangaroo is a sort of alter-ego but</span>
  <span id="freeText1006994296490984979" style="display:none">This book is a collection of sketches about a stand-in for the author an a kangaroo. The kangaroo moves next door and calls himself a Communist. <br />They develop an odd relationship in which Marc-Uwe basically pays for everything and the kangaroo pontificates, weasels and fights against the system, with little effect. The passive Marc-Uwe seems to enjoy the symbiotic friendship that allows him to step out and trespass. Some funny situations ensue. <br />One suspects the Kangaroo is a sort of alter-ego but let's not get carried away. Most situations are quite silly and a few can be funny. I particularly enjoyed a sketch in which the kangaroo has to have its pouch scanned at the airport and a couple of others. After a while, the mischief pursued by the high energy, Hegel quoting, jingoist punching kangaroo and the lethargic, somewhat idiotic and good natured Marc gets a bit repetitive. This is the kind of book people ages 14-18 might enjoy for its irreverence and sense of rebellion.I read it to keep up with current German use but wouldn't pay too much attention to it except as scripted material fro shorts or animation. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1006994296490984979" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16415962058982156969">There's nothing exactly wrong with this book, it is amusing and the level of German is a pretty good fit with my abilities. Each chapter is between 1 and 6 pages long and consists of an anecdote, and initially this shortness was a positive - always something new coming. But this also means there isn't a plot or any character development, thus nothing to keep me coming back to the book. <br/><br/>This is a book I own, so maybe I'll pick it back up somewhere down the line.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('RDhs9in0li+TLDlhpfvGMQYWuZtlz+4YPRv1TPaxuep2+gzeXS0RVXxxq2F2ov6uefnUDLDb81RFoSdFogQaKA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JW9f1of8/lfaC5GRPJF1Wf+wvGxnMc7Ll1lU2OpN+RwXrT/+8yV5LTVWA5HvyE3GgF/R+7Il04fv44bRvvha3g==')})
  }

Waru<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText10959301415498750050\" style=\"display:none\">Warum ist es eigentlich so schwer, über Rassismus zu sprechen?\n\n„Darf ich mal deine Haare anfassen?“, „Kannst du Sonnenbrand bekommen?“, „Wo kommst du her?“ Wer solche Fragen stellt, meint es meist nicht böse. Aber dennoch: Sie sind rassistisch. Warum, das wollen weiße Menschen oft nicht hören.\nAlice Hasters erklärt es trotzdem. Eindringlich und geduldig beschreibt sie, wie Rassismus ihren Alltag als Schwarze Frau in Deutschland prägt. Dabei wird klar: Rassismus ist nicht nur ein Problem am rechten Rand der Gesellschaft. Und sich mit dem eigenen Rassismus zu konfrontieren, ist im ersten Moment schmerzhaft, aber der einzige Weg, ihn zu überwinden.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"10959301415498750050\" href=\"#\" Großartig!« Anne Will.\nSophie Passmann ist Feministin und so gar nicht einverstanden mit der Plattitüde, der alte weiße Mann sei an allem schuld. Sie will wissen, was hinter diesem Klischeebild steckt und fragt nach: Ab wann ist man ein alter weißer Mann? Und kann man vielleicht verhindern, einer zu werden?Sophie Passmann gehört zu einer neuen Generation junger Feministinnen; das sind Frauen, die stolz, laut und selbstbestimmt sind. Sie wollen Vorstandschefinnen werden oder Hausfrauen, Kinder kriegen oder Karriere machen oder beides. Und sie haben ein Feindbild, den alten weißen Mann. Dabei wurde nie genau geklärt, was der alte weiße Mann genau ist. Eines ist klar: Er hat Macht und er will diese Macht auf keinen Fall verlieren. Doch Sophie Passmann will Gewissheit statt billiger Punch-lines, deswegen trifft sie mächtige Männer, um mit ihnen darüber zu sprechen: »Sind Sie ein alter weißer Mann und wenn ja – warum?« Die Texte, Dunkle Magie, Intrigen, Täuschungen, Vertrauen, Freundschaft, Rache und ja, auch die Liebe zeichnen die folgende Geschichte aus.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/2863757.Marc_Uwe_Kling">About Marc-Uwe Kling</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/2863757.Marc_Uwe_Kling"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1358872253p3/2863757.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11035071443692783724">Marc-Uwe Kling wurde geboren. Er studierte an der Großen Akademie von Lagado, wie man ein Haus vom Dach her nach unten baut. Er hat über seinen Mitbewohner, ein kommunistisches Känguru, drei kapitalismuskritische Bücher geschrieben, welche sich total gut verkaufen. Außerdem macht er mit seiner Band „Die Gesellschaft“ Reformhauspunk und am Ende muss wieder der Steuerzahler für alles aufkommen. Hey.</span>
  <span id="freeText11035071443692783724" style="display:none">Marc-Uwe Kling wurde geboren. Er studierte an der Großen Akademie von Lagado, wie man ein Haus vom Dach her nach unten baut. Er hat über seinen Mitbewohner, ein kommunistisches Känguru, drei kapitalismuskritische Bücher geschrieben, welche sich total gut verkaufen. Außerdem macht er mit seiner Band „Die Gesellschaft“ Reformhauspunk und am Ende muss wieder der Steuerzahler für alles aufkommen. Hey. Ho. Let’s go.</span>

              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_40136903').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>
